                margin-left: var(--data--authored-marginleft-desktop);
                margin-right: var(--data--authored-marginright-desktop);
            }

            @media (max-width: 767px) {
            # + .default {
                margin-top: var(--data--authored-margintop-mobile);
                margin-bottom: var(--data--authored-marginbottom-mobile);
                margin-left: var(--data--authored-marginleft-mobile);

</div>
<div class="plain-html base-component parbase aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
   
     
        

    


    <!-- keep following calss for in pageNav to work. -->
    

    
    
    
    


    
	
	<section class="rte-container" data-track-analytics="true">
		
	    
	    <!--Push Down Banner V1 Analytics Patch (3/18/24), remove it if not using v1 -->
<script>
(function ($) {
 if($('.pushdown-banner').length>0){
    console.debug('setting up the patch...');

    // first we try to get the path url
    var setBannerBackgroundClickAnalytics = () => {
        console.debug('running patch...');

        let homepageAnalitycsLocaleCode;
        if (window.location.pathname === "/" || window.location.pathname.includes('/en_us')) {
          homepageAnalitycsLocaleCode = 'en_us';
        } else if (window.location.pathname.includes('/ja_jp')) {
          homepageAnalitycsLocaleCode = 'ja_jp';
        } else if (window.location.pathname.includes('/de_de')) {
          homepageAnalitycsLocaleCode = 'de_de';
        } else if (window.location.pathname.includes('/fr_fr')) {
          homepageAnalitycsLocaleCode = 'fr_fr';
        } else if (window.location.pathname.includes('/ko_kr')) {
          homepageAnalitycsLocaleCode = 'ko_kr';
        } else if (window.location.pathname.includes('/zh_cn')) {
          homepageAnalitycsLocaleCode = 'zh_cn';
        } else if (window.location.pathname.includes('/zh_tw')) {
          homepageAnalitycsLocaleCode = 'zh_tw';
        } 

        const otherLocaleHomepage = (window.location.pathname === "/ja_jp" || window.location.pathname === "/de_de" || window.location.pathname === "/fr_fr" || window.location.pathname === "/ko_kr" || window.location.pathname === "/zh_cn" || window.location.pathname === "/zh_tw");
        const isHomepage = (window.location.pathname === "/" || window.location.pathname.includes('homepage') || otherLocaleHomepage);
        var isPatched = false;

        const targetNode = document.querySelector("body");
        const config = { attributes: false, childList: true, subtree: true };

        const pushDownBannerMutationCallback = (mutationList, pushDownBannerObserver) => {
            for (const mutation of mutationList) {
                if (mutation.type === "childList") {
                    console.debug('more mutations');
                    if (mutation.target.classList.contains('pushdown-banner') && !isPatched) {
                        console.debug('found the pushdownBanner');

                        //do something here
                        pushDownBannerObserver.disconnect();
                        isPatched = true;

                        continueWithThePatching();
                    }
                }
            }
        };

        const sanitizeAnalyticsHref = (ctaHref = '') => {
            // we need to check if this is an absolute or relative link
            var urlPattern = /^https?:\/\//i;
            let finalURL = null;
            if (urlPattern.test(ctaHref)) {
                finalURL = new URL(ctaHref);
            } else {
                finalURL = new URL(`https://${window.location.hostname}/${ctaHref}`);
            }
            
            let linkPathName = finalURL.pathname;
            if (linkPathName.includes('//')) {
                linkPathName = linkPathName.replace('//', '/');
            }

            return `${finalURL.hostname}${linkPathName}`;
        };

        const setAnalyticEvents = (elementContainer = '') => {
            if (elementContainer === null || elementContainer === '' || elementContainer.length === 0) return new Error(`The element passed to the analitycs processor is empty...`);

            const anchorList = elementContainer.querySelectorAll('a');

            anchorList.forEach(anchor => {
                anchor.setAttribute('data-track-analytics', 'false');
                anchor.classList.add('no-analytics');
                //anchor.addEventListener('click', ctaAnalyticsProcess);
            });
        };

        var pushDownBannerObserver = new MutationObserver(pushDownBannerMutationCallback);
        pushDownBannerObserver.observe(targetNode, config);

        var continueWithThePatching = () => {
            let pushDownBannerElementHeight = 0;
            let headerElementHeight = 0;

            const pushDownBannerElement = document.querySelector('#pushdown-banner');
            if (pushDownBannerElement !== null) {
                pushDownBannerElementHeight = pushDownBannerElement.getBoundingClientRect().height;
                setAnalyticEvents(pushDownBannerElement);
            }
            

            const headerElement = document.querySelector('.splunk-header-v2 nav.splunk-navbar');
            if (headerElement !== null) {
                headerElementHeight = headerElement.getBoundingClientRect().height;
            }

            if (pushDownBannerElement !== null && headerElement !== null) {
                const totalHeight = pushDownBannerElementHeight + headerElementHeight;
            let bannerSpecialStyle;

            // Adding some pushdown banner height patch
            const specialCSS = `
                @media (max-width: 767px) {
                    html.hasBanner #splunk-main-content {
                        animation-name: showBannerMobileConfClose !important;
                    }
                    
                    html.hasBanner.showBanner #splunk-main-content {
                        animation-name: showBannerMobileConf !important;
                    }

                    @keyframes showBannerMobileConf {
                        0% {
                            margin-top: 0px;
                        }
                        100% {
                            margin-top: ${totalHeight}px;
                        }
                    }
            
                    @keyframes showBannerMobileConfClose {
                    0% {
                        margin-top: ${totalHeight}px;
                        }
                        100% {
                        margin-top: 0px;
                        }
                    }
                }
                `;

                if (bannerSpecialStyle === undefined){
                    let updatedCSSNode = document.createElement('style');
                    updatedCSSNode.setAttribute('id', "bannerSpecialStyles");
                    updatedCSSNode.textContent = specialCSS;
        
                    document.head.appendChild(updatedCSSNode);
        
                    bannerSpecialStyle = document.querySelector('#bannerSpecialStyles');
        
                } else {
                    bannerSpecialStyle.textContent = specialCSS;
                }
            }

            // Analytics patch
            const getTheBaseURLfromTheButton = (buttonElement = null) => {
                if (buttonElement === null) return new Error(`Push Down banner's button was not found...`);

                //first we get the href from the element
                const originalLink = buttonElement.getAttribute(`href`);

                //Now we assign it into the returning variable
                let processedURL = originalLink.trim();

                //Now we proceed to remove the base of the url 'http://' or 'https://'
                processedURL = processedURL.replace('https://', '');
                processedURL = processedURL.replace('http://', '');

                // Now we proceed to check if the last character is a forward slash
                if (processedURL.endsWith('/')) {
                    processedURL = processedURL.slice(0, -1);
                }

                return processedURL;
            };

            const processAnalyticsComponentName = (ctaText = '') => {
                return ctaText.replaceAll(" ", "-").toLowerCase();
            };

            if (pushDownBannerElement !== null) {
                console.debug('push down banner found, patching click...');
    
                // now we try to get the info from the button assigned
                const psbButtonElementSpan = pushDownBannerElement.querySelector(".pushDownBanner-ctaButton .splunk-btn span");
                const psbButtonElementURL = pushDownBannerElement.querySelector(".pushDownBanner-ctaButton .splunk-btn").getAttribute('href');
                const psbButtonElementText = pushDownBannerElement.querySelector(".pushDownBanner-ctaButton .splunk-btn").innerText;

                const analyticsComponentName = processAnalyticsComponentName(psbButtonElementText);
                console.log('isHomepage',isHomepage);
                if (isHomepage) {
                    $('#pushdown-banner .pushDownBanner-backgroundImageSection').on('click', function () {
                        console.debug('click homepage');
                        window.dataLayer.push({
                        event: "linkClick_hp",
                        eventInfo: {
                            category: "All clicks on CTA Button",
                            eventLabel: `${psbButtonElementSpan.innerHTML}`,
                            clickUrl: `${window.location.hostname}/${homepageAnalitycsLocaleCode}`,
                            component: `pushDownBanner_${analyticsComponentName}_splunk-button`,
                            componentName: "splunk-button",
                            container: "PushDownBanner",
                            destinationUrl: sanitizeAnalyticsHref(psbButtonElementURL),
                            modernization: !0,
                        },
                        });
                    
                        //GA4 DataLayer Push
                        window.dataLayer.push({
                        event: 'link_click_hp',
                        link_text: `${psbButtonElementSpan.innerHTML}`,
                        link_domain: `${window.location.hostname}`,
                        link_url: sanitizeAnalyticsHref(psbButtonElementURL),
                        link_position: 'PushDownBanner',
                        });
                    });
                    $('#pushdown-banner .pushDownBanner-container').on('click', function (event) {
                        console.debug('click homepage');
                        window.dataLayer.push({
                        event: "linkClick_hp",
                        eventInfo: {
                            category: "All clicks on CTA Button",
                            eventLabel: `${psbButtonElementSpan.innerHTML}`,
                            clickUrl: `${window.location.hostname}/${homepageAnalitycsLocaleCode}`,
                            component: `pushDownBanner_${analyticsComponentName}_splunk-button`,
                            componentName: "splunk-button",
                            container: "PushDownBanner",
                            destinationUrl: sanitizeAnalyticsHref(psbButtonElementURL),
                            modernization: !0,
                        },
                        });
                    
                        //GA4 DataLayer Push
                        window.dataLayer.push({
                            event: 'link_click_hp',
                            link_text: `${psbButtonElementSpan.innerHTML}`,
                            link_domain: `${window.location.hostname}`,
                            link_url: sanitizeAnalyticsHref(psbButtonElementURL),
                            link_position: 'PushDownBanner',
                        });
                    });
                } else {
                    $('#pushdown-banner .pushDownBanner-backgroundImageSection').on('click', function () {
                        console.debug('click non homepage');
        
                        window.dataLayer.push({
                        event: "linkClick",
                        eventInfo: {
                            category: "All clicks on CTA Button",
                            eventLabel: `${psbButtonElementSpan.innerHTML}`,
                            clickUrl: `${window.location.hostname}/${homepageAnalitycsLocaleCode}`,
                            component: `pushDownBanner_${analyticsComponentName}_splunk-button`,
                            componentName: "splunk-button",
                            container: "PushDownBanner",
                            destinationUrl: sanitizeAnalyticsHref(psbButtonElementURL),
                            modernization: !0,
                        },
                        });
                    
                        //GA4 DataLayer Push
                        window.dataLayer.push({
                        event: 'link_click',
                        link_text: `${psbButtonElementSpan.innerHTML}`,
                        link_domain: `${window.location.hostname}`,
                        link_url: sanitizeAnalyticsHref(psbButtonElementURL),
                        link_position: 'PushDownBanner',
                        });
                    });
                    $('#pushdown-banner .pushDownBanner-container').on('click', function () {
                        console.debug('click non homepage');
        
                        window.dataLayer.push({
                        event: "linkClick",
                        eventInfo: {
                            category: "All clicks on CTA Button",
                            eventLabel: `${psbButtonElementSpan.innerHTML}`,
                            clickUrl: `${window.location.hostname}/${homepageAnalitycsLocaleCode}`,
                            component: `pushDownBanner_${analyticsComponentName}_splunk-button`,
                            componentName: "splunk-button",
                            container: "PushDownBanner",
                            destinationUrl: sanitizeAnalyticsHref(psbButtonElementURL),
                            modernization: !0,
                        },
                        });
                    
                        //GA4 DataLayer Push
                        window.dataLayer.push({
                        event: 'link_click',
                        link_text: `${psbButtonElementSpan.innerHTML}`,
                        link_domain: `${window.location.hostname}`,
                        link_url: sanitizeAnalyticsHref(psbButtonElementURL),
                        link_position: 'PushDownBanner',
                        });
                    });
                }
        
                console.debug('page patched');
            }
        };
    };

    document.addEventListener('load', setBannerBackgroundClickAnalytics());
}
})(jQuery);
</script>

        <div class="splunkBlogsArticle-body-content">
            <!-- Section 2.2 -->
            <!-- here's where tha parsys should be -->
            <div>




    
    
    <div class="text base-component parbase">
   
     
        

    


    <!-- keep following calss for in pageNav to work. -->
    

    
    
    

<div class="cmp-text rte-container">
    <p><i>Splunk is committed to using inclusive and unbiased language. This blog post might contain terminology that we no longer use. For more information on our updated terminology and our stance on biased language, please visit <a href="https://www.splunk.com/en_us/blog/leadership/biased-language-has-no-place-in-tech-a-follow-up.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">our blog post</a>. We appreciate your understanding as we work towards making our community more inclusive for everyone.</i></p>
<hr />

<p>The Splunk Threat Research Team (STRT) continues to monitor new relevant payloads to the ongoing conflict in Eastern Europe. One of these new payloads was found by the <a href="https://cert.gov.ua/article/39518" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Ukranian CERT</a> named “Industroyer2.” The name of this new payload references the original &#34;<a href="https://collaborate.mitre.org/attackics/index.php/Software/S0001" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Industroyer</a>&#34; malicious payload used against the country of Ukraine&#39;s power grid in 2016 and allegedly was able to affect <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industroyer" target="_blank" rel="noopener">a fifth of the power capacity of the city of</a> Kyiv. </p>
<p>According to the recent <a href="https://cert.gov.ua/article/39518" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Ukraine CERT</a> and <a href="https://www.welivesecurity.com/2022/04/12/industroyer2-industroyer-reloaded/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">ESET</a> report, Industroyer2 resembles the former Industroyer in functionality and is also targeting the electric grid containing commands targeting high-voltage electrical substations. It was reported that Industroyer2 was also used along with <a href="https://www.splunk.com/en_us/blog/security/threat-update-caddywiper.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">CaddyWiper,</a> another payload recently addressed by the Splunk Threat Research Team. This payload — in combination with previous featured destructive payloads — targets <a href="https://www.splunk.com/en_us/blog/security/strt-ta03-cpe-destructive-software.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">CPEs</a>. These customer premise devices such as modems, cable modems, and internet gateways are devices that provide connectivity to the great majority of commercial and residential customers, and speak to the attacker’s intention of overwhelming or degrading the victim&#39;s infrastructure. </p>
<p>The following is an analysis of relevant detection opportunities of this payload and observed <a href="https://www.splunk.com/en_us/blog/learn/ttp-tactics-techniques-procedures.html">TTPs</a> during the deployment of this payload. </p>
<h2>Parameter Check</h2>
<p>The first part of its code is checking parameters that can execute some of its features related to timing and logging. Below is the code screenshot of this checking with its 2 parameters.</p>
<p><img src="/content/dam/splunk-blogs/images/en_us/2022/param-check.png" class="aligncenter"/></p>
<p>The first parameter is “-t” which will trigger a waiting timer relative to the current minute of the system time. For example, if your system time is 14:19:22 PM and you use this parameter with a value of 25 as the third parameter, it means it will wait 5 mins before it executes its code like the screenshot below.</p>
<p><img src="/content/dam/splunk-blogs/images/en_us/2022/timer.png" class="aligncenter"/></p>
<p>While the “-o” parameter is a feature to redirect its console logs to a debug log file you inputted as the 3rd parameter.</p>
<h2>Console Logs</h2>
<p>Upon executing this malware, it outputs some console logs with a customized code structure that tells something about what features it executes. Some of it will be discussed further in the next subheadings. Below is an example of the console logs during its execution.</p>
<p><img src="/content/dam/splunk-blogs/images/en_us/2022/logs-cons.png" class="aligncenter"/></p>
<h2>Terminate Process and Rename Process File Path</h2>
<p>This function enumerates all running processes in the targeted host and looks for the process named “PServiceControl.exe” and also the process name stated in its config data. It will also look for the file path of that process in a specific folder that is in the config file and rename it with “.MZ” file extension.</p>
<p>The code screenshot below shows the process termination and renaming of process file path. We can see in the code snippet the code “RNM” plus the last error code after the call MoveFileA() function that will be displayed in its console logs after executing this part of the code. You can see that in the console log screenshot earlier.</p>
<p><img src="/content/dam/splunk-blogs/images/en_us/2022/terminate-proc.png" class="aligncenter"/></p>
<h2>HardCoded Configuration Data</h2>
<p>This malware contains hardcoded configuration files that will be parsed with the help of CommandLineToArgvW() function and put in a structure that will be used later in its code. Below is the screenshot of the parsing function.</p>
<p><img src="/content/dam/splunk-blogs/images/en_us/2022/parse-config.png" class="aligncenter"/></p>
<p>The config data contains values and checks that this payload  uses through its execution. We saw four main components of its three configuration data settings that are hardcoded to its data section like the screenshot below: The first component is the IP address of devices where it tries to communicate via IEC-104 protocol, the next one is the port number (2404), third is the process name (PService_PPD.exe) it tries to kill aside from “PServicecontrol.exe” and a file path (D:\OIK\DevCounter) where it locates the process file path it tries to kill to rename it with .MZ file extension. </p>
<p><img src="/content/dam/splunk-blogs/images/en_us/2022/config2.png" class="aligncenter"/></p>
<h2>Detections</h2>
<p>Below are the detections related to the Industroyer2 malware and other components found during the attack that was mentioned in the <a href="https://www.welivesecurity.com/2022/04/12/industroyer2-industroyer-reloaded/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">ESET blog</a> and <a href="https://cert.gov.ua/article/39518" target="_blank" rel="noopener">CERT-UA blog</a>.</p>
<h3>Linux Adding Crontab Using List Parameter</h3>
<p>This analytic identifies a suspicious cron jobs modification using crontab list parameters. This command line parameter can be abused by malware like Industroyer2, adversaries, and red teamers to add a crontab entry to their malicious code to execute to the schedule they want.</p>
<pre>
| tstats &#96;security_content_summariesonly&#96; count min(_time) as firstTime max(_time) as lastTime from datamodel&#61;Endpoint.Processes 
</pre>
<pre>
  where Processes.process_name &#61; &#34;crontab&#34; Processes.process&#61; &#34;* -l*&#34; 
</pre>
<pre>
  by  Processes.parent_process_name Processes.process_name Processes.process Processes.process_id Processes.parent_process_id Processes.dest Processes.user
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;drop_dm_object_name(Processes)&#96; 
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;security_content_ctime(firstTime)&#96; 
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;security_content_ctime(lastTime)&#96; 
</pre>
<p><img src="/content/dam/splunk-blogs/images/en_us/2022/crontab-detection.png" class="aligncenter"/></p>
<h3>Linux Deleting Critical Directory Using RM Command</h3>
<p>This analytic identifies a suspicious deletion of a critical folder in Linux machine using rm command. This technique was seen in Industroyer2 campaign to wipe or destroy energy facilities of a targeted sector.</p>
<pre>
| tstats &#96;security_content_summariesonly&#96; count min(_time) as firstTime max(_time) as lastTime from datamodel&#61;Endpoint.Processes 
</pre>
<pre>
  where Processes.process_name &#61;rm AND Processes.process&#61; &#34;* -rf *&#34; AND Processes.process IN (&#34;*/boot/*&#34;, &#34;*/var/log/*&#34;, &#34;*/etc/*&#34;, &#34;*/dev/*&#34;)
</pre>
<pre>
  by Processes.parent_process_name Processes.process_name Processes.process Processes.process_id Processes.parent_process_id Processes.process_guid Processes.dest Processes.user 
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;drop_dm_object_name(Processes)&#96; 
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;security_content_ctime(firstTime)&#96; | &#96;security_content_ctime(lastTime)&#96;
</pre>
<p><img src="/content/dam/splunk-blogs/images/en_us/2022/rm-detections.png" class="aligncenter"/></p>
<h3>Linux Disable Services</h3>
<p>This analytic identifies events that attempt to disable a service. This is typically identified in parallel with other instances of service enumeration of attempts to stop a service and then delete it.</p>
<pre>
| tstats &#96;security_content_summariesonly&#96; count min(_time) as firstTime max(_time) as lastTime from datamodel&#61;Endpoint.Processes 
</pre>
<pre>
  where Processes.process_name IN (&#34;systemctl&#34;, &#34;service&#34;, &#34;svcadm&#34;)  Processes.process &#61; &#34;* disable*&#34; 
</pre>
<pre>
  by Processes.parent_process_name Processes.process_name Processes.process Processes.process_id Processes.parent_process_id Processes.process_guid Processes.dest Processes.user 
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;drop_dm_object_name(Processes)&#96; 
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;security_content_ctime(firstTime)&#96; | &#96;security_content_ctime(lastTime)&#96;
</pre>
<p><img src="/content/dam/splunk-blogs/images/en_us/2022/service-disable-detection.png" class="aligncenter"/></p>
<h3>Linux Shred Overwrite Command</h3>
<p>This analytic identifies a shred process to overwrite files in a linux machine. Shred Linux application is designed to overwrite a file to hide its contents or make the deleted file unrecoverable.</p>
<pre>
| tstats &#96;security_content_summariesonly&#96; count min(_time) as firstTime max(_time) as lastTime from datamodel&#61;Endpoint.Processes 
</pre>
<pre>
  where Processes.process_name &#61;shred AND Processes.process IN (&#34;*-n*&#34;, &#34;*-u*&#34;, &#34;*-z*&#34;, &#34;*-s*&#34;)
</pre>
<pre>
  by Processes.parent_process_name Processes.process_name Processes.process Processes.process_id Processes.parent_process_id Processes.process_guid Processes.dest Processes.user 
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;drop_dm_object_name(Processes)&#96; 
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;security_content_ctime(firstTime)&#96; | &#96;security_content_ctime(lastTime)&#96;
</pre>
<p><img src="/content/dam/splunk-blogs/images/en_us/2022/shred-detection.png" class="aligncenter"/></p>
<h3>Linux Stop Services</h3>
<p>This analytic identifies events that attempt to stop or clear a service. </p>
<p>This is typically identified in parallel with other instances of service enumeration of attempts to stop a service and then delete it.</p>
<pre>
| tstats &#96;security_content_summariesonly&#96; count min(_time) as firstTime max(_time) as lastTime from datamodel&#61;Endpoint.Processes 
</pre>
<pre>
  where Processes.process_name IN (&#34;systemctl&#34;, &#34;service&#34;, &#34;svcadm&#34;)  Processes.process &#61;&#34;*stop*&#34;
</pre>
<pre>
  by Processes.parent_process_name Processes.process_name Processes.process Processes.process_id Processes.parent_process_id 
</pre>
<pre>
  Processes.process_guid Processes.dest Processes.user 
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;drop_dm_object_name(Processes)&#96; | &#96;security_content_ctime(firstTime)&#96; 
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;security_content_ctime(lastTime)&#96;
</pre>
<p><img src="/content/dam/splunk-blogs/images/en_us/2022/service-stop-detection.png" class="aligncenter"/></p>
<h3>Linux High Frequency Of File Deletion In Boot Folder</h3>
<p>This analytic identifies a high frequency of file deletion relative to process name and process id /boot/ folder.</p>
<pre>
| tstats &#96;security_content_summariesonly&#96; values(Filesystem.file_name) as deletedFileNames values(Filesystem.file_path) as deletedFilePath dc(Filesystem.file_path) as numOfDelFilePath count min(_time) as firstTime max(_time) as lastTime 
</pre>
<pre>
  FROM datamodel&#61;Endpoint.Filesystem  
</pre>
<pre>
  where Filesystem.action&#61;deleted Filesystem.file_path &#61; &#34;/boot/*&#34; 
</pre>
<pre>
  by _time span&#61;1h  Filesystem.dest Filesystem.process_guid Filesystem.action 
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;drop_dm_object_name(Filesystem)&#96; 
</pre>
<pre>
  |rename process_guid as proc_guid 
</pre>
<pre>
  |join proc_guid, _time [
</pre>
<pre>
  | tstats &#96;security_content_summariesonly&#96; count FROM datamodel&#61;Endpoint.Processes where Processes.parent_process_name !&#61; unknown 
</pre>
<pre>
  NOT (Processes.parent_process_name IN (&#34;/usr/bin/dpkg&#34;, &#34;*usr/bin/python*&#34;, &#34;*/usr/bin/apt-*&#34;, &#34;/bin/rm&#34;, &#34;*splunkd&#34;, &#34;/usr/bin/mandb&#34;)) 
</pre>
<pre>
  by _time span&#61;1h Processes.process_id Processes.process_name Processes.process Processes.dest Processes.parent_process_name Processes.parent_process Processes.process_path Processes.process_guid 
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;drop_dm_object_name(Processes)&#96; 
</pre>
<pre>
  |rename process_guid as proc_guid 
</pre>
<pre>
  | fields _time dest user parent_process_name parent_process process_name process_path process proc_guid registry_path registry_value_name registry_value_data registry_key_name action] 
</pre>
<pre>
  | table  process_name process proc_guid action _time  deletedFileNames deletedFilePath numOfDelFilePath parent_process_name parent_process  process_path dest user
</pre>
<pre>
  | where  numOfDelFilePath &gt;&#61; 200 
</pre>
<p><img src="/content/dam/splunk-blogs/images/en_us/2022/bulk-deletion.png" class="aligncenter"/></p>
<h3>Windows Processes Killed By Industroyer2 Malware</h3>
<p>This analytic identifies known processes killed by Industroyer2 malware. </p>
<p>This technique was seen in the Industroyer2 malware attack that tries to kill several processes of windows host machines related to the energy facility network.</p>
<pre>
&#96;sysmon&#96; EventCode&#61;5 process_name IN (&#34;PServiceControl.exe&#34;, &#34;PService_PPD.exe&#34;) 
</pre>
<pre>
  | stats min(_time) as firstTime max(_time) as lastTime count by process_name process process_path process_guid process_id EventCode dest user_id
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;security_content_ctime(firstTime)&#96;| &#96;security_content_ctime(lastTime)&#96; 
</pre>
<p><img src="/content/dam/splunk-blogs/images/en_us/2022/terminate-detection.png" class="aligncenter"/></p>
<h3>Windows Hidden Schedule Task Settings</h3>
<p>The following query utilizes Windows Security EventCode 4698. A scheduled task was created to identify suspicious tasks registered on Windows either via schtasks.exe OR TaskService with hidden settings that are unique entry of malware like Industroyer2 or attack that uses lolbin to download other files or payload to the infected machine.</p>
<pre>
&#96;wineventlog_security&#96; EventCode&#61;4698
</pre>
<pre>
  | xmlkv Message
</pre>
<pre>
  | search Hidden &#61; true
</pre>
<pre>
  | stats count min(_time) as firstTime max(_time) as lastTime by  Task_Name, Command, Author, Hidden, dest
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;security_content_ctime(firstTime)&#96; | &#96;security_content_ctime(lastTime)&#96;
</pre>
<p><img src="/content/dam/splunk-blogs/images/en_us/2022/hidden-task-detections.png" class="aligncenter"/></p>
<h3>Windows Linked Policies In ADSI Discovery</h3>
<p>This analytic utilizes PowerShell Script Block Logging (EventCode&#61;4104) to identify the &#96;[Adsisearcher]&#96; type accelerator being used to query Active Directory for domain groups.</p>
<pre>
&#96;powershell&#96; EventCode&#61;4104 ScriptBlockText &#61; &#34;*[adsisearcher]*&#34; ScriptBlockText &#61; &#34;*objectcategory&#61;organizationalunit*&#34; ScriptBlockText &#61; &#34;*findAll()*&#34;
</pre>
<pre>
  | stats count min(_time) as firstTime max(_time) as lastTime by EventCode ScriptBlockText Computer user_id 
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;security_content_ctime(firstTime)&#96;  | &#96;security_content_ctime(lastTime)&#96;
</pre>
<p><img src="/content/dam/splunk-blogs/images/en_us/2022/org-detections.png" class="aligncenter"/></p>
<h3>Windows Root Domain Linked Policies Discovery</h3>
<p>This analytic utilizes PowerShell Script Block Logging (EventCode&#61;4104) to identify the &#96;[Adsisearcher]&#96; type accelerator being used to query Active Directory for domain groups. Red Teams and adversaries may leverage &#96;[Adsisearcher]&#96; to enumerate root domain linked policies for situational awareness and Active Directory Discovery.</p>
<pre>
&#96;powershell&#96; EventCode&#61;4104 ScriptBlockText &#61; &#34;*[adsisearcher]*&#34; ScriptBlockText &#61; &#34;*.SearchRooT*&#34; ScriptBlockText &#61; &#34;*([ADSI]”$_”).gplink*&#34;
</pre>
<pre>
  | stats count min(_time) as firstTime max(_time) as lastTime by EventCode ScriptBlockText Computer user_id 
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;security_content_ctime(firstTime)&#96; 
</pre>
<pre>
  | &#96;security_content_ctime(lastTime)&#96;
</pre>
<p><img src="/content/dam/splunk-blogs/images/en_us/2022/root-detection.png" class="aligncenter"/></p>
<table border="1" width="100%"><tbody><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><b>Type </b></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><b>Name</b></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><b>Technique ID</b></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><b>Tactic</b></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><b>Description</b></p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">TTP</p>
<br />
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/winevent_scheduled_task_created_within_public_path/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">WinEvent Scheduled Task Created Within Public Path</a> (Updated)</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/005/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1053.005</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Execution, Persistence, Privilege Escalation</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">The following query utilizes Windows Security EventCode 4698. A scheduled task was created to identify suspicious tasks registered on Windows either via schtasks.exe OR TaskService with a command to be executed from a user-writable file path.</p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Hunting </p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/winevent_windows_task_scheduler_event_action_started/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">WinEvent Windows Task Scheduler Event Action Started</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/005/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1053.005</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Execution, Persistence, Privilege Escalation</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This hunting analytic assists with identifying suspicious tasks that have been registered and run in Windows using EventID 200 (action run) and 201 (action completed).</p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">TTP </p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/schtasks_run_task_on_demand/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Schtasks Run Task On Demand</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1053</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Execution, Persistence, Privilege Escalation</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic identifies an on-demand run of a Windows Schedule Task through shell or command-line. </p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">TTP </p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/attempted_credential_dump_from_registry_via_reg_exe/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Attempted Credential Dump From Registry via Reg exe</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1003</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Credential Access</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic identifies the use of reg.exe attempting to export Windows registry keys that contain hashed credentials. Adversaries will utilize this technique to capture and perform offline password cracking.</p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">TTP </p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/dump_lsass_via_comsvcs_dll/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Dump LSASS via comsvcs DLL</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/001/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1003.001</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Credential Access</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic identifies the usage of comsvcs.dll for dumping the lsass process.</p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">TTP </p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/executable_file_written_in_administrative_smb_share/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Executable File Written in Administrative SMB Share</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/002/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1021.002</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Lateral Movement</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic identifies executable files (.exe or .dll) being written to Windows administrative SMB shares (Admin$, IPC$, C$).</p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">TTP </p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/suspicious_process_file_path/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Suspicious Process File Path</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1543</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Persistence, Privilege Escalation</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic identifies a suspicious process running in a file path where a process is not commonly seen and is most commonly used by malicious software.</p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">TTP </p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/executables_or_script_creation_in_suspicious_path/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Executables Or Script Creation In Suspicious Path</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">T1036</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Defense Evasion</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic identifies suspicious executables or scripts (known file extensions) in a list of suspicious file paths in Windows.</p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">TTP </p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/impacket_lateral_movement_commandline_parameters/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Impacket Lateral Movement Commandline Parameters</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1021<br />
 </a><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/002/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1021.002<br />
 </a><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/003/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1021.003<br />
 </a><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1047/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1047<br />
 </a><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1543/003/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1543.003</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Lateral Movement<br />
Execution<br />
Persistence, Privilege Escalation</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic identifies the presence of suspicious command line parameters typically present when using Impacket tools.</p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Anomaly</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/linux_system_network_discovery/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Linux System Network Discovery</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">T1016</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Discovery</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic identifies possible enumeration of local <a href="https://www.splunk.com/en_us/blog/learn/network-configuration.html">network configuration</a>. This technique is commonly used as part of recon of adversaries or threat actors to know some network information for its next or further attack. </p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">TTP </p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://splunkresearch.com/endpoint/recon_using_wmi_class/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Recon Using WMI Class</a></p>
<br />
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1592/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1592</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Reconnaissance</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic identifies suspicious PowerShell via EventCode 4104, where WMI is performing an event query looking for running processes or running services. </p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Hunting </p>
</td><td style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/linux_adding_crontab_using_list_parameter/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Linux Adding Crontab Using List Parameter</a> (New)</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/003/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1053.003</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Execution, Persistence, Privilege Escalation</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic identifies a suspicious cron jobs modification using crontab list parameters.</p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">TTP </p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/linux_deleting_critical_directory_using_rm_command/" rel="noopener">Linux Deleting Critical Directory Using RM Command</a> (New)</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1485/" rel="noopener">T1485</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Impact</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic identifies a suspicious deletion of a critical folder in a Linux machine using rm command.</p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">TTP </p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/linux_disable_services/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Linux Disable Services</a> (New)</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1489/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1489</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Impact</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic identifies events that attempt to disable a service.</p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">TTP </p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/linux_shred_overwrite_command/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Linux Shred Overwrite Command</a> (New)</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1485/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1485</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Impact</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic identifies a shred process to overwrite files in a Linux machine.</p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">TTP </p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/linux_stop_services/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Linux Stop Services</a> (New)</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1489/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1489</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Impact</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic identifies events that attempt to stop or clear a service. </p>
<br />
<br />
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Anomaly</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/windows_processes_killed_by_industroyer2_malware/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Windows Processes Killed By Industroyer2 Malware</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1489/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1489</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Impact</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic identifies known processes killed by Industroyer2 malware. </p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">TTP </p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/windows_hidden_schedule_task_settings/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Windows Hidden Schedule Task Settings </a>(New)</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1053</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Execution, Persistence, Privilege Escalation</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This query utilizes Windows Security EventCode 4698. </p>
<p style="	text-align: center;
">A scheduled task was created to identify suspicious tasks registered on </p>
<p style="	text-align: center;
">Windows either via schtasks.exe OR TaskService with a hidden setting.</p>
<br />
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Anomaly</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/windows_linked_policies_in_adsi_discovery/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Windows Linked Policies In ADSI Discovery</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1087/002/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1087.002</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Discovery</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic utilizes PowerShell Script Block Logging (EventCode&#61;4104) to identify the &#96;[Adsisearcher]&#96; type accelerator being used to query Active Directory for domain groups.</p>
</td></tr><tr><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Anomaly</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://research.splunk.com/endpoint/windows_root_domain_linked_policies_discovery/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Windows Root Domain linked policies Discovery</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
"><a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1087/002/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1087.002</a></p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">Discovery</p>
</td><td><p style="	text-align: center;
">This analytic utilizes PowerShell Script Block Logging (EventCode&#61;4104) to identify the &#96;[Adsisearcher]&#96; type to enumerate root domain linked policies for situational awareness and Active Directory Discovery.</p>
<br />
<br />
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>* To see a detailed explanation on the different types please refer to <a href="https://github.com/splunk/security_content/wiki/Detection-Analytic-Types" target="_blank" rel="noopener">this</a> wiki. </i></p>

<h2 style="	padding-top: 15.0px;
">Mitigation</h2>
<p>Please follow <a href="https://www.cisa.gov/news/2020/07/23/protect-operational-technologies-and-control-systems-against-cyber-attacks" target="_blank" rel="noopener">CISA and NSA Joint advisory</a> on securing Operational Technology (OT).</p>
<h2>Learn More</h2>
<p>You can find the latest content about security analytic stories on <a href="https://github.com/splunk/security-content/releases/tag/v3.12.0" target="_blank" rel="noopener">GitHub</a> and in <a href="https://splunkbase.splunk.com/app/3449/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Splunkbase</a>. <a href="https://splunkbase.splunk.com/app/3435/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Splunk Security Essentials</a> also has these detections available via push update. In the upcoming weeks, the Splunk Threat Research Team will be releasing a more detailed blog post on this analytic story. Stay tuned!</p>
<p>For a full list of security content, check out the <a href="https://docs.splunk.com/Documentation/ESSOC/3.21.0/RN/Enhancements" target="_blank" rel="noopener">release notes</a> on <a href="https://docs.splunk.com/Documentation/ESSOC" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Splunk Docs</a>.</p>

                <div class="splunkBlogsAuthorBadge-image">

                </div>
                <div class="splunkBlogsAuthorBadge-authorName"><a href="/en_us/blog/author/secmrkt-research.html">Splunk Threat Research Team </a></div>
                <div class="splunkBlogsAuthorBadge-authorDescription"><p> </p>
<p>The Splunk Threat Research Team is an active part of a customer’s overall defense strategy by enhancing Splunk security offerings with verified research and security content such as use cases, detection searches, and playbooks. We help security teams around the globe strengthen operations by providing tactical guidance and insights to detect, investigate and respond against the latest threats. The Splunk Threat Research Team focuses on understanding how threats, actors, and vulnerabilities work, and the team replicates attacks which are stored as datasets in the <a href="https://github.com/splunk/attack_data/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Attack Data repository</a>. <br />
<span style="	background-color: transparent;
"><br />
 Our goal is to provide security teams with research they can leverage in their day to day operations and to become the industry standard for SIEM detections. We are a team of industry-recognized experts who are encouraged to improve the security industry by sharing our work with the community via conference talks, open-sourcing projects, and writing white papers or blogs. You will also find us presenting our research at conferences such as Defcon, Blackhat, RSA, and many more.</span></p>
<p><br />
Read more <a href="https://github.com/splunk/security_content" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Splunk Security Content</a>. </p>
</div>
